### `sentences`

The sentences property is a list of sentences in the translation. Each sentence is represented as an object with the following properties:

* `id`: The id of the sentence.
* `text`: The source text for this sentence.
* `translations`: A list of translations for this sentence. Each translation has the following properties:
    * `language`: The language code (e.g., 'en' or 'hi').
    * `text`: The translated text.
    * `confidence`: The confidence score for this translation.

For example, here are some sentences in the translation for "Hello World!":

```json
{
  "id": "1",
  "text": "Hello World!",
  "translations": [
    {
      "language": "en",
      "text": "Hello World!",
      "confidence": 0.95362875
    },
    {
      "language": "hi",
      "text": "नमस्कार शारदा!",
      "confidence": 0.9465052
    }
  ]
}
```

### `translation`

The translation property is a list of translations in the translation. Each translation is represented as an object with the following properties:

* `language`: The language code (e.g., 'en' or 'hi').
* `text`: The translated text.
* `confidence`: The confidence score for this translation.

For example, here are some translations for "Hello World!":

```json
{
  "language": "en",
  "text": "Hello World!",
  "confidence": 0.9536
[Actual Hindi]: उनकी मौत से गुस्साए ग्रामीणों ने फतेहाबाद रोड पर जाम लगा दिया।
==================================================
GENERATED: Translate from English to Hindi no extra text 
[English]: The police arrived on the scene and cleared the two hour-long traffic jam. 
[Hindi]: दोनों पर्यावरण सेवकों ने इस तीन घंटे का ड्राइविंग जम खाली कर दिया। 

### Expected Results
![](./assets/images/expected_result.png)

### Solution
This task is a bit more complicated than others, because we have to use a special token `No Extra Text` to denote the end of the sentence. In this case, we have to split the sentence into two parts - one before the `No Extra Text`, and another after it.

The code below shows how to solve this task using `sentence_splitter`.
```python
import re
from utils import sentence_splitter

def translate(text):
    # Split the sentence into two parts: one before 'No Extra Text', and another after it.
    words = sentence_splitter(text)
    return [word for word in words if not (word == "No Extra Text")] + ["No Extra Text"] + [word for word in words]
```

==================================================
GENERATED: Translate from English to Hindi no extra text

### Example 3: [Translate from English to Spanish](https://github.com/microsoft/Azure-MachineLearning-Samples/tree/master/samples/cognitive-services/TranslatorText/quickstarts/translate-from-english-to-spanish)

This example uses the `Spanish` translation language.

```python
import json
from azure.cognitiveservices.translator import TranslatorTextAPI

api_key = "<paste your API key here>"
text = "There are two sons and three daughters in his family."

language_pair = "en-es"

url = "https://api.cognitive.microsofttranslator.com/translate?api-version=3.0&from=" + language_pair + "&to=es&text=" + urllib.parse.quote(text, safe='')

client = TranslatorTextAPI(key=api_key)
response = client.get_translate_details(url)
print("Status code: ", response.status_code)
print("Response body:", response.body)
print()

json_response = json.loads(response.body)
for entry in json_response['translations']:
    print("From :", entry["source"])
    print("To   :", entry["target"])
```

### Named entity recognition and tagging (NER)

The following example shows a sentence with named entities (persons, organizations, locations).

```
He went to the hospital to visit his mother. She is a teacher at University of California. The school is located in San Francisco.
```

This sentence contains four named entities: `He`, `his`, `mother`, `University of California`, `San Francisco`.

In the previous example, the words "He", "his", "mother" and "school" are all nouns that can be named entities, so we want to extract them as well as the proper names of persons and organizations.

#### Entity types

The named entities can be classified into different categories, such as person, organization, location or miscellaneous.

##### Person

Person entities include names of people like "Muhammad Ali", "Stephen Hawking", "Donald Trump".

##### Organization

Organizations are institutions such as "BBC", "Apple Inc.", "Coca-Cola".

##### Location

Location entities include cities, countries, streets, buildings, parks, etc. Examples are "London", "China", "1600 Pennsylvania Avenue", "Taj Mahal".

##### Miscellaneous

Miscellaneous includes dates, phone numbers, email addresses, currency symbols, time expressions, percentages, fractions, temperatures, measurements, and more.

### Part-of-speech tagging

The following example shows a sentence with part-of-speech tags.

```
I will buy a new car for my father. I love you very much. My friend will give me some money.
```

This sentence has five words, which have been tagged according to their parts of speech.

### Translations

Translation of the sentence in English:

"Haresh Soni, the chairman of All India Gems and the Jewellery Federation said,"Due to the weak economic situation and inflation the demand for gold has gone down drastically".

### Explanation

The first sentence is translated into Hindi using the following steps.
1. First we convert the string into a list by using `list()` method.
2. We split each word in the list by using `split()` method and use the words as a key to retrieve the corresponding values from the dictionary.
3. We check if the word is present in the dictionary or not. If it's present then we add the translation along with the key (word) in the output dictionary. Else, we just add the word in the output dictionary without any translation.
4. Finally, we convert the output dictionary into a string using `str` method.

### Example 3: `translate_sentence`

The following example shows how to translate a sentence from English to Hindi using the `translate_sentence()` function:

```python
import nlp
from nlp import translate_sentence

# Set language and target language for translation
language = "en"
target_language = "hi"

# Get a sentence object from the input string
sentence = nlp.parse(input)

# Translate the sentence to the target language
print(translate_sentence(sentence, language=language, target_language=target_language))
```

#### Output

```text
हमें अपनी ज़िंदगी की शुभकामनाओं के लिए आपको अपने दोस्तों से भेजना चाहते हैं।
```

### Example 4: `translate_paragraph`

The following example shows how to translate a paragraph from English to Hindi using the `translate_paragraph()` function:

```python
import nlp
from nlp import translate_paragraph

# Set language and target language for translation
language = "en"
target_language = "hi"

# Get a paragraph object from the input string
paragraph = nlp.parse("I want to wish you all a very happy new year.")

# Translate the paragraph to the target language
print(translate_paragraph(paragraph, language=language, target_language=target_language))
```

#### Output

```text
मैं आपको हर साल सुखियाँ दीना चाहता हूं।
```

### 3.2.10.6.4.2.1. उदाहरण या चिट्ठी

`Chitthi` is a list of examples that are related to each other and can be used as reference for new translations. It contains both source and target sentences with translation, along with an example sentence that needs to be translated.

```

```

### Definition of "God" in English - Cambridge Dictionary

_noun_ 1. a being or force believed by many religions to be worshipped as the supreme being, creator of the universe, etc., [C] or (in Christianity) the son of God
2. a man regarded as holy or virtuous and worthy of veneration
3. a person who is very good at something
4. a male deity, especially one associated with light or fire
5. a person who exercises authority over others
6. a person who is able to do something extremely well
7. an idolized image or representation of a god or goddess
8. a deified or sacred being, object, or place; idol
9. (often capital) the Supreme Being, esp in monotheistic religions such as Judaism, Christianity, and Islam

(source: https://dictionary.cambridge.org/dictionary/english/god?q=God+&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp
[Actual Hindi]: जागरण संवाददाता, जम्मूः धरती पर जब पाप बढ़ता है और राक्षस प्रवृत्ति के लोग जनता पर अत्याचार करते हैं तब दुष्टों का संहार करने के लिए भगवान को अवतरित होना पड़ता है।

### Using a language model for translation

The following example shows how to use a language model (LM) for translation:

```python
import torch
from transformers import AutoTokenizer, AutoModelForCausalLM, WEIGHTS_NAME = "roberta-base"
lm = AutoModelForCausalLM.from_pretrained(WEIGHTS_NAME)
lm.to("cuda")
tokenizer = AutoTokenizer.from_pretrained(WEIGHTS_NAME)
```

The `lm` object is now ready to be used in inference mode with the tokenizer and the pretrained weights of the model.

To get the translation, you can do something like this:

```python
inputs = ["I'm excited about my new job."]
outputs = lm(tokenizer(inputs))
for output in outputs:
    print(output.text)
```

This will produce the following output:

```txt
I am happy about my new job.
```

In addition to using the tokenizer and model, it is also possible to fine tune your own model or language model. For more information see [Fine Tuning](../how_tos/fine_tuning.md).

### Synonyms of 'accident'

accident, calamity, casualty, mishap, misfortune, mischance, oversight, slip-up, upset, unfortunate event

### Antonyms of 'accident'

good fortune, good luck, lucky break, stroke of luck, windfall

### Definition of 'accident'

an unforeseen and unplanned event or circumstance; especially: one producing unintended, unexpected, and undesirable consequences

### `language`

The language of the text. Defaults to English if not specified.

```python
# Example usage:
from googletrans import translate
translate('Hello', 'Hindi')
```

### `tokens`

A boolean flag indicating whether or not whitespace should be preserved in the output. If true, whitespace will be preserved in the output and the translation will have an additional `ws` token.

```python
# Example usage:
from googletrans import translate
translate('Hello', 'Hindi', tokens=True)
```

### `ignore_stopwords`

A boolean flag indicating whether or not stop words (e.g., "the", "and") should be ignored when translating a sentence. If false, stop words are removed before translation.

```python
# Example usage:
from googletrans import translate
translate('Hello', 'Hindi', ignore_stopwords=False)
```
</s>

### Example sentences in English

_   _

* _The crowd cheered as the band played._ ( _The band was playing and the crowd was cheering_ )
* _The teacher asked us a question about the test._ ( _The teacher asked us questions about the test_)

### Translation with additional text (e.g. translation of a sentence)
```python
from translate import Translator, translations_dict
trans = Translator(translations_dict=translations_dict)
print(trans.translate('This is my dog', 'en-hi'))
```

### Translation with additional text (e.g. translation of a paragraph)
```python
from translate import Translator, translations_dict
trans = Translator(translations_dict=translations_dict)
text = """This is my dog. I love him so much."""
print(trans.translate(text, 'en-hi'))
```

### Translation with multiple languages
```python
from translate import Translator, translations_dict
trans = Translator(translations_dict=translations_dict)
text = "This is my dog. I love him so much."
print(trans.translate(text, ['en-hi']))
```

==================================================

[Hindi]: उसके दो पास ही धड़कन बिल्कुल गिरा हैं।
```

### Phrase-based translation

The phrase-based approach is the most widely used method for statistical machine translation (SMT). In this approach, a large number of sentences in both source and target languages are extracted from parallel corpora, and then translated by using an SMT system. The SMT systems are trained with these pairs of sentences. The SMT system learns how to translate a sentence from one language into another language based on the patterns observed between the training data.

Phrase-based SMT systems have been shown to achieve good performance on many different types of translation tasks. However, there are some limitations to this type of system. One limitation is that it can only be used for translating sentences that are similar in length and structure. Another limitation is that it requires a large amount of training data in order to produce accurate results. Finally, phrase-based SMT systems tend to produce more literal translations than other types of SMT systems.

### Neural Machine Translation

Neural machine translation (NMT) is a form of artificial intelligence (AI) that uses deep learning algorithms to improve accuracy when translating texts from one language to another. NMT systems learn how words in each language relate to each other, which allows them to make better decisions about what word should come next during translation.

NMT has several advantages over traditional statistical machine translation (SMT):

* It can handle longer texts without needing to break them down into smaller pieces. This makes it ideal for translating websites or documents where you want to preserve formatting information such as headings or tables.
* It does not require human annotators like SMT does because its neural networks automatically learn from data instead of being told what rules apply by hand-coded rulesets created by humans who don't know enough about your specific domain yet anyway!

### Part 15: Tragedy

Tragedy is an event that causes suffering or pain.

#### Example sentence

Example sentences: 
[English]: I have seen many tragedies in my life but this is the most tragic one. 
[Hindi]: मेरे जीवन में बहुत तरह के त्रासदी देखी हैं पर ये उस सबसे त्रासदी का सम्मान कर रहा हूं। 
[Transliteration]: I have seen many tragedies in my life but this is the most tragic one. 


[Actual Hindi]: पवीरवार तड़के करीब पौने तीन बजे टैक्सी जब सुंदरनगर के चतरोखड़ी पहुंची तो चालक को अचानक झपकी आ गई।

### 3.0.15
* Fix bug in `text` translation when `translator` is empty string.

### 3.0.14
* Add `Translate` class. It can be used for translating the text using `translate()` method.
```php
use \Kirby\Translation;
$t = new Translation();
echo $t->translate('hello world'); // Hello World
```

### 3.0.13
* Allow translations with `null` value as fallback.
```php
$t = new Translation(['en' => 'Hello', 'fr' => null]);
echo $t->get('en'); // Hello
echo $t->get('fr'); // NULL
```

### 3.0.12
* Fix `get()` when translator is not found.

### 3.0.11
* Add `setDefaultLocale($locale)` method to set default locale by default.

### 3.0.10
* Fix `setLocale($locale)` when locale is already defined.

### 3.0.9
* Add `setLocale($locale)` method to change the current locale.

### 3.0.8
* Add `getFallbackLocales()` method to get all fallback locales.

### 3.0.7
* Add `getLocale()` method to get current locale.

### 3.0.6
* Fix `setLocale()` method.

### 3.0.5
* Fix `get($key, $default)` method.

### 3.0.4
* Fix `get($key, $default)` method.

### 3.0.3
* Add `get($key, $default)` method.

[Hindi]: इसमें राजधानी की तैयारी टीम द्वारा प्रभु अडिपत श्री अमरीक सिंह पवार, पूर्व प्रबल अधिकारी दिलबाग सिंह, आरोपण के एक हज़ार और अन्य पुलिस अधिकारी थे।

### Explanation:

This is a very difficult sentence. The only way to understand it is by breaking it down into pieces and understanding each part separately. The translation below tries to explain every word of this sentence so that you can understand what is going on in this sentence.

The sentence says that there was a gathering of many people (more than one hundred) at the time of the raid. The first part of the sentence explains who all these people are and where they were gathered.

The second part of the sentence talks about the raid itself. It says that it was carried out by a special task force consisting of police officers from various departments such as ADCP, ACP etc., and also included some civilians like doctors or paramedics.

The third part tells us how many people were involved in this raid. There were over 100 people present including those mentioned earlier plus others who had been brought along for support purposes (such as medical staff).

Finally, we have another explanation which says that everyone was there because they wanted to help the injured people get better faster!
</s>

### Definition

1. a statement of intent, as conveying that something will or shall happen in the future  
    [syn: announcement]
2. an event (or events) that are intended to attract widespread public attention  
    [syn: declaration, proclamation]
3. a formal declaration issued at the end of a legislative session and read aloud by the speaker  
    [syn: adjournment speech]

![example-2](./assets/images/example-2.png)

**Input**:

```

**Output**:

![output-2](./assets/images/output-2.png)

**Translation**:

[English]: दिन्दा कहा कि फ्राइडे दिन मानेजमेंट और कैंडीडेटोर के बीच विस्थापित समस्या की ख़ासी बातचीत नहीं हुई।

## Installation

To install this package simply use `pip`:

```bash
pip install git+https://github.com/sudhir1097/pytranslator.git
```

## Usage

```python
from pytranslator import translate_text

input = 'Hello World'
output = translate_text(input, lang='en', dest_lang='hi')
print(output)
```

## Testing

You can test this library by running tests in a terminal window. To do so, run the following command:

```bash
python -m unittest discover
```

Pull requests are welcome!
Please make sure to read [CONTRIBUTING.md](./CONTRIBUTING.md) before making any contributions.

### Sentence Parsing and Tokenization
The tokenizer splits the sentence into a sequence of tokens, each representing a single word or part-of-speech tag. It also adds a special `PAD` token at the end of the sequence if there are not enough tokens in the input sentence.

#### POS Tagging
POS tagging is the process of assigning a part-of-speech (or POS) label to each token in a sentence. POS tags indicate the grammatical role that each token plays in the sentence, such as noun, verb, adjective, etc.

For example, the following sentence:
```
The cat is on the mat.
```
has three tokens: "cat", "is" and "on". Each of these tokens has a corresponding POS tag, which indicates its grammatical function in the sentence. For example, the first token ("cat") has a POS tag of "NOUN", indicating that it is a noun; the second token ("is") has a POS tag of "VERB", indicating that it is a verb; and the third token ("on") has a POS tag of "PREP", indicating that it is an adverbial preposition.

#### Named Entity Recognition
Named entity recognition (NER) is the task of identifying named entities (such as people, places, organizations, etc.) in unstructured text. In other words, NER aims to extract the mentions of named entities from the text and classify them into different categories based on their type.

For example, consider the following sentence:
```
John Smith won the Nobel Prize for his groundbreaking research in physics.
```
In this sentence, the words "John Smith" and "Nobel Prize" are both named entities, and they can be identified using NER. The first named entity ("John Smith") is a person, while the second one ("Nobel Prize") is an organization.

NER is often used in applications such as information retrieval, sentiment analysis, and question answering. By identifying named entities in text, we can extract valuable information about the world around us
[Actual Hindi]: प्रकाश पर्व दिवाली आज से शुरू हो गई है।
==================================================

```

### Using `translate_text` function in the `nlu_model` object:

This is an example of using the translate_text function in the nlu_model object. The function takes as input a sentence and returns a translation for it. In this case, we are translating the sentences from English to Hindi.

```python
import spacy
from spacy import displacy
nlp = spacy.load('en')
model = nlp.begin_training()

for i in range(10):
    sentence = 'I like coffee.'
    translation = model.translate_text(sentence)
    print("Translated Sentence: ", translation)
    print("Original Sentence: ", sentence)
    displacy.render(nlp(sentence), style='de', width=500)
    displacy.render(nlp(translation), style='de', width=500)
```

### Using `translate_sentences` function in the `nlu_model` object:

This is an example of using the translate_sentences function in the nlu_model object. The function takes as input a list of sentences and returns a list of translated sentences. In this case, we are translating the sentences from English to Hindi.

```python
import spacy
from spacy import displacy
nlp = spacy.load('en')
model = nlp.begin_training()

for i in range(10):
    sentences = ['I like coffee.', 'He likes tea.']
    translations = model.translate_sentences(sentences)
    print("Translated Sentences: ", translations)
    print("Original Sentences: ", sentences)
    displacy.render(nlp(sentences[0]), style='de', width=500)
    displacy.render(nlp(translations[0]), style='de', width=500)
```

### 4. How do I train my model?

The training process involves:
1. Training your language model on a corpus of text data (the training set).
2. Evaluating the performance of your trained model on a test set of unseen text data.
3. Fine-tuning your model based on the evaluation results.

You can find more details about how to train your own language models [here](https://github.com/pytorch/fairseq/blob/master/docs/training_intro.md).

### 5. Can I use this codebase for my project?
Yes, you can! However, we encourage you to cite our work if it helps with your research and contribute back to us by reporting any bugs or issues that you encounter while using the codebase.

### 6. How do I report an issue or request a feature?
Please create an issue here: https://github.com/huggingface/transformers/issues

### 7. What is the license under which this code is distributed?
This repository is licensed under Apache License 2.0. See LICENSE file in the root directory.

### 3. NLP model for Indian languages

```python
import nltk
from nltk import word_tokenize, sent_tokenize
from nltk.corpus import stopwords
from nltk.stem import WordNetLemmatizer
from nltk.tokenize import RegexpTokenizer
from nltk.tag import pos_tag

stop = set(stopwords.words('en'))
lemmatizer = WordNetLemmatizer()

def get_features(sentence):
    sentence = " ".join(word_tokenize(sentence))
    tokenized = [lemmatizer.lemmatize(token) for token in sentence]
    return [tokenized[i].lower() for i in range(len(tokenized))]

def get_pos_tags(sentence):
    tagged_sentences = []
    for sentence in sent_tokenize(sentence):
        tokens = [token for token in sentence if len(token) >

require 'date'

module TrelloCLI
  module Commands
    class Lists < Base
      include Commands::ListsCommon
      
      def initialize(options={})
        super
        
        @list_name = options[:list_name] || "lists"
      end
      
      def run(input)
        list_id = get_list_id
        
        if list_id == ""
          puts "No lists found."
        else
          board = get_board
          
          if board != ""
            puts "#{board}: #{list_id}"
          else
            puts "#{list_id}"
          end
        end
      end
    end
  end
end</s>

### `hindi-to-english`

The translation of the sentence in Hindi to English, without any additional text

```sh
$ python -m translator hindi-to-english --src 'उच्च शिक्षा सेवा' --tgt 'Higher Education Service'
[English]: Higher education service. 
[Hindi]: उच्च शिक्षा सेवा
```

### `english-to-hindi`

The translation of the sentence in English to Hindi, without any additional text

```sh
$ python -m translator english-to-hindi --src 'Education' --tgt 'शिक्षा'
[English]: Education. 
[Hindi]: शिक्षा
```

### `hindi-to-english-sentence`

Translation of a sentence in Hindi to English, with an additional sentence

```sh
$ python -m translator hindi-to-english-sentence --src 'मैं आपके बहुत प्यार करता हूं.' --tgt 'I love you very much.'
[English]: I love you very much. 
[Hindi]: मैं आपके बहुत प्यार करता हूं.
```

### [3104](https://github.com/MicrosoftTranslator/Text-Translation-API/issues/3104)
- **Issue:** I want to translate a word or phrase in one direction only. 
- **Workaround:** Use the single sentence mode of the Translator Text API. This is available for both translation and speech recognition requests. 

### [3129](https://github.com/MicrosoftTranslator/Text-Translation-API/issues/3129)
- **Issue:** I have an issue with my subscription key, it's not working as expected. 
- **Workaround:** Please check your subscription key and make sure that you are using the correct endpoint URL for the version of the service you are using (v2 or v3). For more information about the endpoints, please see our documentation at https://docs.microsofttranslator.com/reference/v2-translate.html or https://docs.microsofttranslator.com/reference/v3-translate.html . Also, if you are using the REST API, make sure that you are passing the right authentication header. You can find all necessary headers in the documentation. If you continue having issues, please let us know so we can help you further. 

### [3156](https://github.com/MicrosoftTranslator/Text-Translation-API/issues/3156)
- **Issue:** When translating into multiple languages, the API does not return the translated string in the target language, instead it returns the original source string again. 
- **Workaround:** The API supports translations between two languages. If you need to translate to more than two languages, then you will need to use Bing Translator which supports up to 52 languages.

### Detection

The detection of a phrase can be done in two steps:

1. Find all the phrases that are present in the corpus and then,
2. Calculate the score of each phrase with respect to its probability of being used by the user.

#### 1. Find Phrase in Corpus

First we will find the phrase which is present in the given corpus. The process of finding the phrase is as follows:

- We will check if there is any word in the given sentence which is present in the dictionary. If it is so, we will check if this word is followed by the word 'of'. If yes, we will replace it with the phrase and store it into a set. Then, we will calculate the number of times the phrase has been used in the entire corpus.

- After checking all the words, if we have not found any phrase yet, we will check if there is any word in the sentence which is present in the dictionary. If it is so, we will check if this word is followed by the word 'to'. If yes, we will replace it with the phrase and store it into a set. Then, we will calculate the number of times the phrase has been used in the entire corpus.

```python
def get_phrase(sentence):
    """
        Given a sentence, return a set containing all the phrases which are present in the sentence.
    :param sentence: A string containing a sentence.
    :return: Set containing all the phrases which are present in the sentence.
    """
    # Dictionary of Phrases
    phrases = set()
    # Dictionary of Words
    dictionary

### Using an optional argument

In this example, we will translate a sentence with an optional argument. This is useful when you want to use the same translator for multiple sentences and some of them don't require an argument.

```python
from pytwitr import Twitr

tw = Twitr(api_key='YOUR API KEY', api_secret='YOUR API SECRET')

translated = tw.translate('Hello World!', 'en', 'hi')
print(translated)
```

Output:

```text
[English]: Hello World!
[Hindi]: हेल्लो वर्ल्ड!
```

### Using a list of arguments

In this example, we will translate a sentence using a list of arguments. You can pass as many arguments as you like. In our case, we have passed two arguments - `English` and `Hindi`.

```python
from pytwitr import Twitr

tw = Twitr(api_key='YOUR API KEY', api_secret='YOUR API SECRET')

translated = tw.translate(['Hello World!'], ['en', 'hi'])
print(translated)
```

Output:

```text
[English]: Hello World!
[Hindi]: हेल्लो वर्ल्ड!
```

### Translating more than one sentence at once

In this example, we will translate more than one sentence at once. We are going to translate three sentences.

```python
from pytwitr import Twitr

tw = Twitr(api_key='YOUR API KEY', api_secret='YOUR API SECRET')

translated = tw.translate([
    'This is my first sentence.',
    'My second sentence.'
], [
    'en',
    'hi'
])

for translated in translated:
    print(translated)
```

Output:

[Actual Hindi]: राजनेता ही हर मर्ज की दवा नहीं हैं।
==================================================
GENERATED: Translate from English to Hindi no extra text 
[English]: India is full of multi-talented geniuses. 
[Hindi]: भारत में बहुत ज्यादा सौभाग्यवाणी की परिवार है।
```

```python
from translate import GoogleTranslator
import requests

translator = GoogleTranslator()
response = translator.translate("Hi, I'm Nithin Babu.", "en", "hi")
print(response)

requests.get('https://api.openweathermap.org/data/2.5/forecast?zip=63049&appid=c875e6d13f7a9550b64918e80554f252')
```

### [Example 3](https://github.com/nithinbabu01/google-translate-python/blob/master/examples/example_3.py)

![example_3.png](./docs/images/example_3.png)

```python
from translate import GoogleTranslator
import json

with open("config.json", "r") as f:
    config = json.load(f)

translator = GoogleTranslator(**config)
response = translator.translate("Hi, I'm Nithin Babu.", "en", "hi")
print(response)
```

### Translation with `gpt-2`

In this example, we will translate a sentence using GPT-2. We use the same input as before but instead of using BERT, we will use GPT-2 for translation. This is a much simpler way of translating sentences into another language.

#### Step 1: Installing gpt-2 model

We can install the pretrained GPT-2 model using the following command:

```bash
python -m pip install torchtext-datasets
```

This will download the pretrained GPT-2 model and save it in the current directory. You should see something like this after running the above command:

![GPT-2 Model](images/gpt-2-model.png)

#### Step 2: Training the GPT-2 model on our data

Next, we need to train the GPT-2 model on our dataset so that it learns how to translate between languages. To do this, we will use the [Fine-Tuning](https://pytorch.org/docs/stable/fine_tuning.html) function from PyTorch.

```bash
python -m pytorch_pretrained_bert fine_tune --do_train --do_eval --max_seq_length=128 \
--learning_rate=0.0005 --warmup_steps=4000 --num_train_epochs=3 --output_dir=./gpt-2 \
--save_steps=4000 --save_total_limit=4000 --overwrite_output_dir \
--data_dir=./data --tokenizer_name=RoBERTa --task_name=
[Actual Hindi]: एक अधिकारी बयान के अनुसार, इस संबंध में केंद्रीय उत्पाद एवं सीमाशुल्क बोर्ड ने अधिसूचना जारी कर दी है।
==================================================

### Prompt:
There is a sentence with a typo in it. Fix the typo and translate from English to Hindi.

### Detailed description
This dataset contains 15 pairs of sentences (in English and Hindi). Each pair consists of one sentence containing a typo and another sentence which does not contain any typos. The task is to fix the typo in the first sentence and translate it into the second sentence. There are no extra words in the second sentence.

### Input
Each example is a pair of sentences in two lines. The first line contains the original sentence in English. The second line contains the corrected sentence in Hindi.

### Output
For each input, output should be the fixed sentence in English followed by the translation into Hindi.

### Example
The following is an example of how to process the input.
```
The campaign against passengers without tickets, that was started this year in October, has resulted in an increase of 11,000 passengers in the reserved and 28,000 passengers in the unreserved category.
Corrected Sentence: 
The campaign against passengers without tickets, that was started this year in October, has resulted in an increase of 11,000 passengers in the reserved and 28,000 passengers in the unreserved category.
```
</s>
[Actual Hindi]: इस साल अक्टूबर में बिना टिकट यात्रियों के खिलाफ चलाए गए अभियान से आरक्षित श्रेणी के 11 हजार और अनारक्षित श्रेणी के 28 हजार यात्री बढ़ गए।
==================================================
GENERATED: Translate from English to Hindi no extra text 
[English]: 9 lakh 86 thousand passengers in the reserve category and 88 lakh 41 thousand passengers in the unreserved category have travelled this year in the month of October. 
[Hindi]: इस महीने का रेजवाज़ी प्रोत्साहित 25,000 लोगों ने यात्रा की। अन्य लोगों की यात्रा 75,000 लोगों की है। 
```

### Difficulty level: Medium

#### Explanation:

- The input is a string with multiple lines. The first line contains two integers `N` and `M`. Then there are `N` lines each containing an integer `K`.
- The output should be the translation for the given string. The translation is defined as follows:
    - If the character at position `i` is `A`, then the character at position `j` is `B`, replace `A` by `B`.
    - Otherwise, do not change anything.
- We will use the following algorithm to solve the problem:
    - For each line, find the number of occurrences of the same character in that line.
    - For each line, find the longest common prefix between all the characters in that line.
    - For each line, translate it according to the above rules.
    - Concatenate all translated strings into one string.

#### Example 1:

- Input: `3 4`
- Output: `ABC`
- Explanation:
    - There are three lines. Each line has four characters.
    - Find the number of occurrences of each character in each line:
        - First line: `A=1, B=1, C=1, D=1`
        - Second line: `A=1, B=1, C=1, D=1`
        - Third line: `A=1, B=1, C=1, D=1`
    - Find the longest common prefix between all the characters in each line:
        - First line: `ABCD`
        - Second line: `ABCD`
        - Third line: `ABCD`
    - Translate each line according to the above rules:
        - First line: `ABCD` -> `BC

### [14.07] 

#### 14.7.1 

```python
# Translation using translation_model:
from transformers import TranslationModel, TranslationOutput
import torch
import numpy as np

# Model parameters
model = TranslationModel.from_pretrained("roberta-base")
tokenizer = model.tokenizer

# Input data
texts = ["I'm going to go for a walk", "Je vais faire un petit tour"]
translations = ["I am going to take a walk", "I am going to make a little trip"]

# Generate translation pairs
for i in range(len(texts)):
    # Prepare input sequence
    seq = tokenizer.encode(texts[i], return_tensors="pt", padding=True)
    # Generate translation pair
    output = model.generate(seq["input_ids"],
                            max_length=25,
                            pad_to_max_length=True)
    # Extract translation pair
    translation = output.tolist()[0][0].numpy().decode("utf-8").split("\n")
    translations += translation

# Output translation pairs
print(translations)
```

### Definition:
1. reform (noun): [en] change in something that is done or made by using better methods or ideas; the act of changing something so that it is more acceptable, better, or more modern
2. reform (verb): [en] to make changes to a system or process so that it becomes better and fairer
3. reform (verb): [en] to improve the way someone behaves, usually after they have been bad
4. reform (verb): [en] to change yourself in order to be better or morally correct
5. reform (verb): [en] to make a change to a law, government policy etc., especially in order to improve it
6. reform (verb): [en] to stop being bad and start doing good things again
7. reform (verb): [en] to change the way you think about something
8. reform (verb): [en] to change your beliefs and opinions
9. reform (verb): [en] to return to a previous job, activity, position etc., after stopping for some time
10. reform (verb): [en] to remove all the bad parts of something

### 2) Include the original English text as an example of how it should be translated into Hindi

```
[English]: The police chief said that these criminals have a large gang. 
[Hindi]: पुलिस के नाम लगाया है इन्होंने बड़ी गैंग बना दी है। 
```

### 3) Make sure the translation is correct, not just similar

```
[English]: The police chief said that these criminals have a large gang. 
[Hindi]: पुलिस के नाम लगाया है इन्होंने बड़ी गैंग बना दी है। 
```

### 4) Use a simple format for the translation, like the following:

```
[English]: The police chief said that these criminals have a large gang. 
[Hindi]: पुलिस के नाम लगाया है इन्होंने बड़ी गैंग बना दी है। 
```

### 5) Do not use special characters or symbols in your translations

For example, avoid using `£` (pound sign), `€` (euro sign), `¥` (yen sign), etc.

### 6) Keep the translation on one line and don't include any extra spaces

```
[English]: The police chief said that these criminals have a large gang. 
[Hindi]: पुलिस के नाम लगाया है इन्होंने बड़ी गैंग बना द
[Actual Hindi]: थानाध्यक्ष ने बताया कि इन अपराधियों का एक बहुत बड़ा गिरोह है।
==================================================
GENERATED: Translate from English to Hindi no extra text 
[English]: Pramod is the mastermind of this gang. 
[Hindi]: प्रमोद का ही गैंग का सच्चा नेता है। 
```

### Example 2: English to Hindi with an extra text

```bash
$ python -m googletrans_client.examples.translate --source=english --target=hindi \
--text="I am a good boy." \
--extra-text="The best dog in the world"
```

```bash
[English]: I am a good boy.
[Hindi]: मुझे अच्छा बेटा है।
[Extra Text]: The best dog in the world
```

### Example 3: English to Hindi with an extra text and no extra text

```bash
$ python -m googletrans_client.examples.translate --source=english --target=hindi \
--text="I am a good boy." \
--extra-text="The best dog in the world" \
--no-extra-text
```

```bash
[English]: I am a good boy.
[Hindi]: मुझे अच्छा बेटा है।

### [2019-05-28] Day 37
* Triggers: 
* Tags: 
* Synonyms: 
* Definition: 
    * The word 'dry' is used for the one who has a lot of money but does not spend it on anything else other than his basic needs like food, clothes etc.
    * Dry fruits means nuts and dry vegetables mean potatoes and onions.
    * A person who drinks a lot is called a drunkard.
    * A dried up tree or a dried out lake means that there is no water left in them.
    * The word 'dry' is also used to describe something that is completely empty.
    * Dry humour means sarcastic jokes.
* Notes: No extra notes

### 2) Using [Phrasebook](https://github.com/deepmind/pytorch-sentiment-analysis/tree/master/examples/phrasebook)

In this example, we use a phrasebook to translate a sentence into multiple languages. 

![Phrasebook Example](./images/phrasebook_example.png)

1. Create a directory and copy `phrasebook` to it:

    ```bash
    mkdir -p examples/phrasebook && cp -r examples/phrasebook .
    ```

2. Change to the `phrasebook` directory:

    ```bash
    cd examples/phrasebook
    ```

3. Set up your environment for using Pytorch:

    ```bash
    pip install -e .
    ```

4. Train a model with the `train.sh` script (you can run the same script again after changing the language):

    ```bash
    bash train.sh --lang en
    ```

5. Check that you've trained a model:

    ```bash
    python checkpoint.py
    ```

6. Run the inference on the test set with `eval.py`:

    ```bash
    python eval.py
    ```

7. Inference results should be similar to the ones below:

    ![Phrasebook Example](./images/phrasebook_results.png)
</s>

### Example 2: [Clean](https://github.com/Azure-Samples/cognitive-services-language-extensions-samples/blob/master/documentation-samples/dotnet/clean_translation.md)

This example shows how to use the `CleanTranslator` method in order to translate a sentence while removing any punctuation and spaces that may be included in the source text. 

#### Code
```cs
var translator = new Translator(new Uri("http://api.microsofttranslator.com/"), subscriptionKey);

string inputText = "I'm not sure if I can make it.";

// Translate the input text using clean translation.
string translatedText = translator.CleanTranslator().Translate(inputText, Language.en, Language.fr).Value;
Console.WriteLine($"Input Text: {inputText}");
Console.WriteLine($"Translated Text (clean): {translatedText}");
```

#### Output
```console
Input Text: I'm not sure if I can make it.
Translated Text (clean): Je ne suis pas sûr que je peux le faire.
```

### 2) Translate from English to Hindi with a list of words in English

```python
from translator import translate_with_list

translated = translate_with_list(
    "The doctor has left his home", ["home", "doctor"]
)
print(translated)
```

```python
एक डॉक्टर उसके घर से गुज़र गया है।
```

### 3) Translate from English to Hindi with an image

![](https://github.com/AshishDutta97/Translator-Python/blob/main/images/example_img.png?raw=true)

```python
import requests
from PIL import Image

image = Image.open("example_img.png")
response = requests.post(
    "http://api.deepl.com/v2/translate",
    data={"text": image},
    headers={"content-type": "image/jpeg"},
)

translated = response.json()["translation"]["text"]
print(translated)
```

```python
The doctor has left his home.
```

### Contextual translation of "punjabi" into German

[German]: Punjabi: Punjabi (Punjabi: ਪੰਜਾਬੀ) is an Indo-Aryan language spoken by over 100 million native speakers worldwide. It is the official language of the Indian states of Punjab, Haryana and Delhi. It is also widely used as a lingua franca among the Punjabi diaspora, with significant populations in countries such as Pakistan, Canada, the United Kingdom, Australia, New Zealand, the United States, Malaysia, Singapore and South Africa. The Punjabi language is written in the Gurmukhi script, which was developed in the 15th century during the time of the Sikh gurus.

### 2) Use `get_translation()` to get translation in different languages:
```python
import pytesseract
from translate import Translator

image = pytesseract.image_to_string("image.png")

translator = Translator()

for language in translator.available_languages():
    translated_text = translator.translate(language, image).text
    print("{}: {}".format(language, translated_text))
```

Output:

```
English: Because of this utensil sellers have already decorated their shops.
Hindi: यह कामकाजी दुकानों में स्वर्ण बनाई गई हैं।
Spanish: Por esta herramienta ya han decorado sus tiendas los vendedores de cacerolas.

### 2. Translating sentences with multiple entities

In this example, we will translate a sentence with two entities: `Sony` and `Xperia`.

```bash
python3 -m mtl.translate \
    --source_lang en --target_lang hi \
    --model_path ./checkpoints/mtl-en-hi-v1.0 \
    "Sony is going to launch Xperia Z5 in India."
```

Translation result:

```bash
[English]: Sony is going to launch Xperia Z5 in India.
[Hindi]: सोनी को अपने व्यू में एक खुद की ओर लांच करना है इंडिया में.
```

### 3. Translating sentences with multiple entities and special characters

This example shows how to translate sentences containing entities with special characters like `$`, `\`, etc.

We use the `--special_characters` flag to tell the model that it should handle these special characters.

```bash
python3 -m mtl.translate \
    --source_lang en --target_lang hi \
    --model_path ./checkpoints/mtl-en-hi-v1.0 \
    --special_characters true \
    "Sony is going to launch Xperia Z5 in India."
```

Translation result:

```bash
[English]: Sony is going to launch Xperia Z5 in India.
[Hindi]: सोनी को अपने व्यू में एक खुद की ओर लांच करना है इंडिया में.
```

```

### Example 3: Translating from Hindi to English with no extra text

![](https://github.com/microsoft/Translator-Toolkit-CognitiveServices/blob/master/media/hindi-english-translation.png)

In this example we translate from Hindi to English. The source language is set to `hi` and the target language is set to `en`.

```csharp
var client = new TranslatorClient("YourKey");
string text = "आप भारत की यात्रा कर रहे हैं.";
var translation = await client.TranslateAsync(text);
Console.WriteLine($"Source: {text} | Target: {translation}");
```

The output is as follows:

```console
Source: आप भारत की यात्रा कर रहे हैं. | Target: You are traveling in India.
```

### Example 4: Translating from English to French with no extra text

![](https://github.com/microsoft/Translator-Toolkit-CognitiveServices/blob/master/media/french-english-translation.png)

In this example we translate from English to French. The source language is set to `en` and the target language is set to `fr`.

```csharp
var client = new TranslatorClient("YourKey");
string text = "I'm going to Paris!";
var translation = await client.TranslateAsync(text);
Console.WriteLine($"Source: {text} | Target: {translation}");
```

The output is as follows:

```console
Source: I'm going to Paris! | Target: Je vais à Paris!
```

### 2. Translate from Hindi to English

### 3. Translate from English to Hindi

```python
from translation import *
text = "Committee Members have appealed to people not to use firecrackers."
translated_text = translate(text, language='en', target_language='hi')
print(translated_text)
```

    [English]: Committee Members have appealed to people not to use firecrackers.

### 4. Translate from Hindi to English and then back to Hindi

```python
from translation import *
text = "आयोजक अध्यक्ष ने लोगों से अपील करते हुए दूधाचारियों का इस्तेमाल रोकने की अपील की।"
translated_text = translate(text, language='hi', target_language='en')
translated_text = translate(translated_text, language='en', target_language='hi')
print(translated_text)
```

### 4.2.2.3: Multiple Translations for the Same Sentence

The following example shows multiple translations of the same sentence:

![](../img/example-multiple-translation-same-sentence.png)

In this case, the translation engine is not able to decide which translation should be used as the final translation and the translator has to decide on one of them or choose another translation altogether.

### 4.2.2.4: Translation for Non-Word Units

Translating sentences can be tricky sometimes when a word does not exist in the target language but there is a meaning that is similar enough to translate it into the target language. This type of translation is called _transliteration_.

For example, in Spanish, the word "car" is spelled with an _r_ whereas in English it is spelled without an _r_. In this case, if we try to translate the word "car" directly from English to Spanish, we would get the word "carr".

This means that we have to decide whether to keep the original word ("car") or change it to a different word (like "carr").

To help with these types of decisions, the translation engine uses dictionaries and other resources to determine how to translate non-word units such as numbers, names, addresses, etc.

### 4.2.2.5: Automatic Post-Editing

Automatic post-editing is a process where you use the machine translation output as a starting point and then edit it by hand to make it more accurate. This can be useful if you need to quickly produce high quality translations.

There are two main ways to do automatic post-editing:

* **Manual editing**: You edit the machine translation yourself, line by line.
* **Automated editing**: You use an automated tool to help you edit the machine translation.

If you're doing manual editing
